46:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":["The Bradley-Terry model's application to human preference learning assumes that human judgments form a ",["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"total order"}]," (transitivity: if A > B and B > C, then A > C) that is ",["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"consistent and independent"}]," of context. In practice, human preferences on complex reasoning tasks (math, code, scientific writing) are often intransitive, context-dependent, and irreproducible across annotators. The model's popularity in RLHF stems not from empirical validation of its assumptions but from mathematical convenience: it leads to a tractable maximum likelihood objective and has been validated post-hoc on simpler preference tasks (summarization quality, toxicity avoidance). For alignment tasks (honesty, helpfulness, safety), the gap between the model's assumptions and human judgment is substantial and remains underexplored."]}]

60:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":["The terminal reward is the RM score minus the KL penalty at the final token; all\nintermediate steps receive only the per-token KL penalty. ",["$","$L2b",null,{"term":"PPO"}],"'s clipped surrogate\nobjective and GAE are then applied to this reward signal, with the language model\nserving as the actor and a separate value head (or a copy of the language model with\nan added scalar head) serving as the critic. This formulation was pioneered by Ouyang et al. (2022) in the InstructGPT paper, which demonstrated that supervised fine-tuning followed by reward modeling and PPO optimization produces significant improvements in human preference ratings over the base SFT model. The empirical gains—especially in reducing harmful outputs and improving instruction-following—validated the RLHF pipeline as a practical approach to alignment, though the paper's ablations did not isolate the contribution of each stage, leading to continued debate about the necessity of the RM stage versus simpler preference optimization."]}]

71:["$","h2",null,{"id":"variants-and-extensions","className":"heading-linked","style":{"fontFamily":"var(--font-display)","fontWeight":600,"fontSize":"1.375rem","color":"var(--text-strong)","letterSpacing":"-0.01em","lineHeight":1.25,"marginBottom":"0.6em","marginTop":"2.5em","paddingBottom":"0.4em","borderBottom":"1px solid var(--border-subtle)","scrollMarginTop":"90px"},"children":["Variants and extensions",["$","$L2c",null,{"id":"variants-and-extensions"}]]}]
72:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":[["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"Constitutional AI (CAI)"}]," (Bai et al., 2022) replaces human preference annotators with the model itself:\nthe model critiques its own responses according to a set of principles (the\n\"constitution\") and generates revised responses. A reward model is then trained on\nthese model-generated preference pairs rather than human-annotated ones. CAI reduces\nthe cost of preference data collection and enables alignment at scales where human\nannotation is impractical. The core contribution of CAI is demonstrating that AI-generated preference pairs can approximate human preferences at a fraction of the cost, shifting the alignment bottleneck from annotation to constitution design. However, the approach replaces the question \"what do humans prefer?\" with \"what does our constitution imply?\", shifting rather than solving the preference specification problem."]}]
73:["$","p",null,{"style":{"fontSize":"1rem","color":"var(--text-body)","lineHeight":1.75,"marginBottom":"1.25em","marginTop":0},"children":[["$","strong",null,{"style":{"color":"var(--text-strong)","fontWeight":600},"children":"RLAIF"}]," (",["$","$L2b",null,{"term":"RL"}]," from AI Feedback) generalizes CAI: the evaluator model can be a separate,\nstronger ",["$","$L2b",null,{"term":"LLM"}],". Preferences are generated by the evaluator rather than humans, then used\nto train the reward model for the policy. RLAIF can be applied iteratively: the policy\nimproves, the evaluator generates harder preference pairs, the RM improves, the policy\nimproves further. This self-improvement loop has achieved human-competitive alignment\nat reduced annotation cost. As of 2025–2026, RLAIF has been scaled to large models (DeepSeek-R1 uses a variant) and shown that iterative self-improvement via synthetic preference data can rival or exceed human-annotated RLHF on reasoning tasks."]}]
